[1mNAME[0m[m
       usermod - modify a user account[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[m
       [1musermod [22m[[4moptions[24m] [4mLOGIN[0m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The [1musermod [22mcommand modifies the system account files.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       The options which apply to the [1musermod [22mcommand are:[m
[m
       [1m-a[22m, [1m--append[0m[m
           Add the user to the supplementary group(s). Use only with the[m
           [1m-G [22moption.[m

       [1m[7m-e[27m[22m, [1m-[7m-e[27m[1mxpiredate [4m[22mEXPIRE_DATE[0m[m
           The date on which the user account will be disabled. The date[m
           is specified in the format [4mYYYY-MM-DD[24m. Integers as input are[m
           interpreted as days after 1970-01-01.[m
[m
           An input of -1 or an empty string will blank the account[m
           expiration field in the shadow password file. The account[m
           will remain available with no date limit.[m
[m
           This option requires a /etc/shadow file. A /etc/shadow entry[m
           will be created if there were none.[m
[m
       [1m-f[22m, [1m--inactive [4m[22mINACTIVE[0m[m
           defines the number of days after the password exceeded its[m
           maximum age during which the user may still login by[m
           immediately replacing the password. This grace period before[m
           the account becomes inactive is stored in the shadow password[m
           file. An input of 0 will disable an expired password with no[m
           delay. An input of -1 will blank the respective field in the[m

[?2004l[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=[4mPS[24m(1)                         User Commands                        [4mPS[24m(1)[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       ps - report a snapshot of the current processes.[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mps [22m[[4moptions[24m][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mps [22mdisplays information about a selection of the active[m
       processes.  If you want a repetitive update of the selection and[m
       the displayed information, use [1mtop [22minstead.[m
[m
       This version of [1mps [22maccepts several kinds of options:[m
[m
       1   UNIX  options, which may be grouped and must be preceded by a[m
           dash.[m
       2   BSD options, which may be grouped and must not be used with a[m
           dash.[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       3   GNU long options, which are preceded by two dashes.[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       Options of different types may be freely mixed, but conflicts can[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       appear.   There  are   some   synonymous   options,   which   are[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       functionally   identical,  due  to  the  many  standards  and  [1mps[0m[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       implementations that this [1mps [22mis compatible with.[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       By default, [1mps [22mselects all processes with the same effective user[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 9 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       ID (euid=EUID) as the current user and associated with  the  same[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 10 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       terminal  as  the invoker.  It displays the process ID (pid=PID),[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 11 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       the  terminal  associated  with  the  process  (tname=TTY),   the[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 12 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       cumulated  CPU  time in [DD-]hh:mm:ss format (time=TIME), and the[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 13 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       executable name (ucmd=CMD).  Output is unsorted by default.[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 14 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 15 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       The use of BSD-style options will add process  state  (stat=STAT)[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 16 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       to  the  default display and show the command args (args=COMMAND)[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 17 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       instead of the executable name.  You can override this  with  the[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 18 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1mPS_FORMAT  [22menvironment  variable.   The  use of BSD-style options[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 19 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       will also change the process selection to  include  processes  on[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 20 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       other  terminals  (TTYs) that are owned by you; alternately, this[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 21 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       may be described as setting the selection to be the  set  of  all[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 22 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       processes  filtered  to exclude processes owned by other users or[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 23 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       not on a terminal.  These effects are not considered when options[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 24 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       are  described  as  being  "identical"  below,  so  [1m-M  [22mwill   be[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       ps - report a snapshot of the current processes.[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mps [22m[[4moptions[24m][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mps [22mdisplays information about a selection of the active[m
       processes.  If you want a repetitive update of the selection and[m
       the displayed information, use [1mtop [22minstead.[m
[m
       This version of [1mps [22maccepts several kinds of options:[m
[m
       1   UNIX  options, which may be grouped and must be preceded by a[m
           dash.[m
       2   BSD options, which may be grouped and must not be used with a[m
           dash.[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[Kuu[Kss[Kee[Krr[K[1;1H[4mPS[24m(1)                         User Commands                        [4mPS[24m(1)[m
[2;1H[m
[3;1H[1mNAME[0m[m
[4;1H       ps - report a snapshot of the current processes.[m
[5;1H[m
[6;1H[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[7;1H       [1mps [22m[[4moptions[24m][m
[8;1H[m
[9;1H[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
[10;1H       [1mps [22mdisplays information about a selection of the active[m
[11;1H       processes.  If you want a repetitive update of the selection and[m
[12;1H       the displayed information, use [1mtop [22minstead.[m
[13;1H[m
[14;1H       This version of [1mps [22maccepts several kinds of options:[m
[15;1H[m
[16;1H       1   UNIX  options, which may be grouped and must be preceded by a[m
[17;1H           dash.[m
[18;1H       2   BSD options, which may be grouped and must not be used with a[m
[19;1H           dash.[m
[20;1H[1;1H[4mPS[24m(1)                         [7mUser[27m[24m Commands                        [4mPS[24m(1)[m
[2;1H[m
[3;1H[1mNAME[0m[m
[4;1H       ps - report a snapshot of the current processes.[m
[5;1H[m
[6;1H[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[7;1H       [1mps [22m[[4moptions[24m][m
[8;1H[m
[9;1H[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
[10;1H       [1mps [22mdisplays information about a selection of the active[m
[11;1H       processes.  If you want a repetitive update of the selection and[m
[12;1H       the displayed information, use [1mtop [22minstead.[m
[13;1H[m
[14;1H       This version of [1mps [22maccepts several kinds of options:[m
[15;1H[m
[16;1H       1   UNIX  options, which may be grouped and must be preceded by a[m
[17;1H           dash.[m
[18;1H       2   BSD options, which may be grouped and must not be used with a[m
[19;1H           dash.[m
[20;1H[K[7m Manual page ps(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       By default, [1mps [22mselects all processes with the same effective [7muser[27m[m
       ID (euid=EUID) as the current [7muser[27m and associated with  the  same[m
       terminal  as  the invoker.  It displays the process ID (pid=PID),[m
       the  terminal  associated  with  the  process  (tname=TTY),   the[m
       cumulated  CPU  time in [DD-]hh:mm:ss format (time=TIME), and the[m
       executable name (ucmd=CMD).  Output is unsorted by default.[m
[m
       The use of BSD-style options will add process  state  (stat=STAT)[m
       to  the  default display and show the command args (args=COMMAND)[m
       instead of the executable name.  You can override this  with  the[m
       [1mPS_FORMAT  [22menvironment  variable.   The  use of BSD-style options[m
       will also change the process selection to  include  processes  on[m
       other  terminals  (TTYs) that are owned by you; alternately, this[m
       may be described as setting the selection to be the  set  of  all[m
       processes  filtered  to exclude processes owned by other [7muser[27ms or[m
       not on a terminal.  These effects are not considered when options[m
       are  described  as  being  "identical"  below,  so  [1m-M  [22mwill   be[m
       considered identical to [1mZ [22mand so on.[m
[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 27 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K       Except   as   described  below,  process  selection  options  are[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 28 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K       additive.  The default  selection  is  discarded,  and  then  the[m
       selected  processes  are  added  to  the  set  of processes to be[m
       displayed.  A process will thus be shown if it meets any  of  the[m
       given selection criteria.[m
[m
[1mEXAMPLES[0m[m
       To see every process on the system using standard syntax:[m
          [1mps -e[0m[m
          [1mps -ef[0m[m
          [1mps -eF[0m[m
          [1mps -ely[0m[m
[m
       To see every process on the system using BSD syntax:[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 41 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
          [1mps -eo e[7muser[27m[1m,r[7muser[27m[1m,s[7muser[27m[1m,f[7muser[27m[1m,f,comm,label[0m[m
          [1mps axZ[0m[m
          [1mps -eM[0m[m
[m
       To see every process running as root (real & effective ID) in[m
       [7muser[27m format:[m
          [1mps -U root -u root u[0m[m
[m
       To see every process with a [7muser[27m-defined format:[m
          [1mps -eo pid,tid,class,rtprio,ni,pri,psr,pcpu,stat,wchan:14,comm[0m[m
          [1mps axo stat,euid,ruid,tty,tpgid,sess,pgrp,ppid,pid,pcpu,comm[0m[m
          [1mps -Ao pid,tt,[7muser[27m[1m,fname,tmout,f,wchan[0m[m
[m
       Print only the process IDs of syslogd:[m
          [1mps -C syslogd -o pid=[0m[m
[m
       Print only the name of PID 42:[m
          [1mps -q 42 -o comm=[0m[m

[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       crypt — storage format for hashed passphrases and available hash‐[m
       ing methods[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The  hashing methods implemented by [4mcrypt[24m(3) are designed only to[m
       process user passphrases for storage and authentication; they are[m
       not suitable for use as general-purpose cryptographic hashes.[m
[m
       Passphrase hashing is not a replacement for  strong  passphrases.[m
       It  is  always possible for an attacker with access to the hashed[m
       passphrases to guess and check  possible  cleartext  passphrases.[m
       However,  with a strong hashing method, guessing will be too slow[m
       for the attacker to discover a strong passphrase.[m
[m
       All of the hashing methods use a “salt” to perturb the hash func‐[m
       tion, so that the  same  passphrase  may  produce  many  possible[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       hashes.   Newer  methods  accept  longer  salt strings.  The salt[m
       should be chosen at random for each user.  Salt defeats a  number[m
       of attacks:[m
[m
       1.   It  is  not possible to hash a passphrase once and then test[m
            it against each account's stored hash; the hash  calculation[m
            must be repeated for each account.[m
[m
       2.   It is not possible to tell whether two accounts use the same[m
            passphrase without successfully guessing one of the phrases.[m
[m
       3.   Tables  of precalculated hashes of commonly used passphrases[m
            must have an entry for each possible salt, which makes  them[m
            impractically large.[m
[m
       All of the hashing methods are also deliberately engineered to be[m
       slow;  they  use  many  iterations of an underlying cryptographic[m
       primitive to increase the cost of each guess.  The newer  hashing[m
       methods  allow the number of iterations to be adjusted, using the[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 20 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       “CPU time cost” parameter to  [4mcrypt_gensalt[24m(3).   This  makes  it[m
       possible to keep the hash slow as hardware improves.[m
[m
[1mFORMAT OF HASHED PASSPHRASES[0m[m
       All of the hashing methods supported by [4mcrypt[24m(3) produce a hashed[m
       passphrase  which  consists  of four components: [4mprefix[24m, [4moptions[24m,[m
       [4msalt[24m, and [4mhash[24m.  The prefix controls which hashing method  is  to[m
       be   used,   and   is   the   appropriate   string   to  pass  to[m
       [4mcrypt_gensalt[24m(3) to select that method.  The contents of [4moptions[24m,[m
       [4msalt[24m, and [4mhash[24m are up to the method.  Depending  on  the  method,[m
       the [4mprefix[24m and [4moptions[24m components may be empty.[m
[m
       The  [4msetting[24m argument to [4mcrypt[24m(3) must begin with the first three[m
       components of a valid hashed passphrase, but anything after  that[m
       is  ignored.   This  makes  authentication simple: hash the input[m
       passphrase using the stored passphrase as the setting,  and  then[m
       compare the result to the stored passphrase.[m
[m
       Hashed  passphrases  are  always entirely printable ASCII, and do[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 39 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       not contain any whitespace or the characters ‘[1m:[22m’, ‘[1m;[22m’, ‘[1m*[22m’,  ‘[1m![22m’,[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 40 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       or  ‘[1m\[22m’.   (These  characters  are used as delimiters and special[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 41 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       markers in the [4mpasswd[24m(5) and [4mshadow[24m(5) files.)[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 42 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 43 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       The syntax of each component of a hashed passphrase is up to  the[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 44 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       hashing  method.   ‘[1m$[22m’ characters usually delimit components, and[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 45 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       the salt and hash are usually encoded as  numerals  in  base  64.[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 46 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       The  details of this base-64 encoding vary among hashing methods.[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 47 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       The common “base64” encoding specified by RFC 4648 is usually [4mnot[0m[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 48 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       used.[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 49 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 50 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mAVAILABLE HASHING METHODS[0m[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 51 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       This is a list of [4mall[24m the hashing methods supported by  [4mcrypt[24m(3),[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 52 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       in  decreasing  order of strength.  Many of the older methods are[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 53 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       now considered too weak to use for new passphrases.   The  hashed[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 54 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       passphrase  format is expressed with extended regular expressions[m

[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 56 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       tions, salt, and hash.[m
[7m Manual page crypt(5) line 57 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       usermod - modify a user account[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[m
       [1musermod [22m[[4moptions[24m] [4mLOGIN[0m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The [1musermod [22mcommand modifies the system account files.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       The options which apply to the [1musermod [22mcommand are:[m
[m
       [1m-a[22m, [1m--append[0m[m
           Add the user to the supplementary group(s). Use only with the[m
           [1m-G [22moption.[m
[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m-b[22m, [1m--badname[0m[m

[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m-c[22m, [1m--comment [4m[22mCOMMENT[0m[m

[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           normally modified using the [1mchfn[22m(1) utility.[m

[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m-d[22m, [1m--home [4m[22mHOME_DIR[0m[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 9 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           The user's new login directory.[m

[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 13 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           created if it does not already exist. If the current home[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 14 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           directory does not exist the new home directory will not be[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 15 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           created.[m

[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 17 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m-e[22m, [1m--expiredate [4m[22mEXPIRE_DATE[0m[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 18 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           The date on which the user account will be disabled. The date[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 19 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           is specified in the format [4mYYYY-MM-DD[24m. Integers as input are[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 20 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           interpreted as days after 1970-01-01.[m

[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 24 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           will remain available with no date limit.[m

[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 30 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           defines the number of days after the password exceeded its[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 31 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           maximum age during which the user may still login by[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 32 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           immediately replacing the password. This grace period before[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 33 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           the account becomes inactive is stored in the shadow password[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 34 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           file. An input of 0 will disable an expired password with no[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 35 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           delay. An input of -1 will blank the respective field in the[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 36 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           shadow password file. See [1mshadow[22m(5) for more information.[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 37 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
           This option requires a /etc/shadow file. A /etc/shadow entry[m
           will be created if there were none.[m
[m
       [1m-g[22m, [1m--gid [4m[22mGROUP[0m[m
           The name or numerical ID of the user's new primary group. The[m
           group must exist.[m
[m
           Any file from the user's home directory owned by the previous[m
           primary group of the user will be owned by this new group.[m
[m
           The group ownership of files outside of the user's home[m
           directory must be fixed manually.[m
[m
           The change of the group ownership of files inside of the[m
           user's home directory is also not done if the home dir owner[m
           uid is different from the current or new user id. This is a[m
           safety measure for special home directories such as /.[m
[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 56 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       [1m-G[22m, [1m--groups [4m[22mGROUP1[24m[[4m,GROUP2,...[24m[[4m,GROUPN[24m]]][m
           A list of supplementary groups which the user is also a[m
           member of. Each group is separated from the next by a comma,[m
           with no intervening whitespace. The groups must exist.[m
[m
           If the user is currently a member of a group which is not[m
           listed, the user will be removed from the group. This[m
           behaviour can be changed via the [1m-a [22moption, which appends the[m
           user to the current supplementary group list.[m
[m
       [1m-l[22m, [1m--login [4m[22mNEW_LOGIN[0m[m
           The name of the user will be changed from [4mLOGIN[24m to [4mNEW_LOGIN[24m.[m
           Nothing else is changed. In particular, the user's home[m
           directory or mail spool should probably be renamed manually[m
           to reflect the new login name.[m
[m
       [1m-L[22m, [1m--lock[0m[m
           Lock a user's password. This puts a '!' in front of the[m
           encrypted password, effectively disabling the password. You[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 75 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           can't use this option with [1m-p [22mor [1m-U[22m.[m
[m
           Note: if you wish to lock the account (not only access with a[m
           password), you should also set the [4mEXPIRE_DATE[24m to [4m1[24m.[m
[m
       [1m-m[22m, [1m--move-home[0m[m
           moves the content of the user's home directory to the new[m
           location. If the current home directory does not exist the[m
           new home directory will not be created.[m
[m
           This option is only valid in combination with the [1m-d [22m(or[m
           [1m--home[22m) option.[m
[m
           [1musermod [22mwill try to adapt the ownership of the files and to[m
           copy the modes, ACL and extended attributes, but manual[m
           changes might be needed afterwards.[m
[m
       [1m-o[22m, [1m--non-unique[0m[m

       [1m-o[22m, [1m--non-unique[0m[m
           allows to change the user ID to a non-unique value.[m
[m
           This option is only valid in combination with the [1m-u [22moption.[m
           As a user identity serves as key to map between users on one[m
           hand and permissions, file ownerships and other aspects that[m
           determine the system's behavior on the other hand, more than[m
           one login name will access the account of the given UID.[m
[m
       [1m-p[22m, [1m--password [4m[22mPASSWORD[0m[m
[7m Manual page usermod(8) line 102 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           defines a new password for the user. PASSWORD is expected to[m
           be encrypted, as returned by [1mcrypt [22m(3).[m
[m
           [1mNote: [22mAvoid this option on the command line because the[m
           password (or encrypted password) will be visible by users[m
           listing the processes.[m
[m
           The password will be written in the local /etc/passwd or[m
           /etc/shadow file. This might differ from the password[m
           database configured in your PAM configuration.[m
[m
           You should make sure the password respects the system's[m
           password policy.[m
[m
       [1m-r[22m, [1m--remove[0m[m
           Remove the user from named supplementary group(s). Use only[m
           with the [1m-G [22moption.[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       groupadd - create a new group[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[m
       [1mgroupadd [22m[[4mOPTIONS[24m] [4mNEWGROUP[0m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The [1mgroupadd [22mcommand creates a new group account using the values[m
       specified on the command line plus the default values from the[m
       system. The new group will be entered into the system files as[m
       needed.[m
[m
       Groupnames may contain only lower and upper case letters, digits,[m
       underscores, or dashes. They can end with a dollar sign. Dashes[m
       are not allowed at the beginning of the groupname. Fully numeric[m
       groupnames and groupnames . or .. are also disallowed.[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       On Debian, the only constraints are that groupnames must neither[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       start with a dash ('-') nor plus ('+') nor tilde ('~') nor[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       contain a colon (':'), a comma (','), or a whitespace (space:' ',[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       end of line: '\n', tabulation: '\t', etc.).[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       On Ubuntu, the same constraints as Debian are in place, with the[m
       additional constraint that the groupname cannot be fully numeric.[m
       This includes octal and hexadecimal syntax.[m
[m
       Groupnames may only be up to 32 characters long.[m
[m

           [1m-g[22m, and the specified GID already exists, another (unique)[m
           GID is chosen (i.e.  [1m-g [22mis turned off).[m
[m

           unless the [1m-o [22moption is used. The value must be non-negative.[m
           The default is to use the smallest ID value greater than or[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 26 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           equal to [1mGID_MIN [22mand greater than every other group.[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 27 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page groupadd(8) line 28 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           See also the [1m-r [22moption and the [1mGID_MAX [22mdescription.[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       groupmod - modify a group definition on the system[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[m
       [1mgroupmod [22m[[4moptions[24m] [4mGROUP[0m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The [1mgroupmod [22mcommand modifies the definition of the specified[m
       [4mGROUP[24m by modifying the appropriate entry in the group database.[m

[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
